# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# etcd Raft Snapshot Too Old on Node Rejoin

## Your Task

An etcd node fails to rejoin a cluster with 'ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable'. Find the Go source files in etcd-io/etcd that (1) define ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable and (2) implement the snapshot availability check during Raft log catch-up.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

45-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully identified the relevant Go source files in etcd-io/etcd that define and implement the snapshot availability check during Raft log catch-up.

## Summary

I found the key components related to `ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable` and the snapshot availability check:

**Definition:**
- **`raft/storage.go` (lines 36-38)**: Defines `ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable` as a sentinel error returned by the Storage interface when a required snapshot is temporarily unavailable.

**Snapshot Availability Check Chain:**
1. **`raft/raft.go` `maybeSendAppend()` (lines 432-489)**: When a leader needs to replicate log entries to a follower but finds the entries have been compacted, it attempts to retrieve a snapshot (line 453).

2. **`raft/log.go` `snapshot()` (lines 204-209)**: This method checks for pending unstable snapshots first, then delegates to the storage layer via `l.storage.Snapshot()`.

3. **Error Handling in `raft/raft.go` (lines 455-457)**: When `ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable` is returned, the leader logs a debug message and defers sending the snapshot, allowing time for the storage layer to prepare it.

This mechanism is critical for the rejoin scenario where an etcd node falls too far behind during a cluster outage and must use snapshot-based recovery to catch up.

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json`.

This error is used in the context of Raft log catch-up when a follower node needs to restore from a snapshot.\\n\\nThe error's primary usage occurs during the snapshot availability check in the Raft log catch-up process. When a leader node (in raft/raft.go) calls the maybeSendAppend() function (lines 432-489), it attempts to replicate log entries to a follower. If the follower's next required log index is too far behind (has been compacted and incorporated into a snapshot), the leader cannot send individual log entries. Instead, it must send a snapshot.\\n\\nThe flow works as follows:\\n\\n1. In maybeSendAppend() (raft/raft.go:432-489), the leader attempts to get the required term and entries from the raftLog (lines 440-441).\\n\\n2. If either the term or entries retrieval fails (line 446: errt != nil || erre != nil), this indicates the requested log index has been compacted. The leader then needs to send a snapshot instead.\\n\\n3. To obtain the snapshot, the leader calls r.raftLog.snapshot() (line 453), which is defined in raft/log.go (lines 204-209).\\n\\n4. The raftLog.snapshot() function first checks if there's a pending unstable snapshot. If not, it delegates to the storage layer by calling l.storage.Snapshot() (line 208).\\n\\n5. If the storage layer returns ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable (checked in raft/raft.go:455), this means the snapshot is not yet ready to be sent. The leader logs a debug message and returns false without sending the snapshot (lines 455-457), allowing the node to retry later.\\n\\nThis mechanism prevents a rejoin scenario where a node falls too far behind and requires snapshot-based recovery, but the snapshot is not yet available (perhaps still being prepared by the storage layer). The error signals that the Storage implementation needs more time to prepare the snapshot, and the Raft state machine should retry the operation later.\"\n}\n",
